Liability for Prior Use of a Pledged Item: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on liability for prior unauthorised use of a pledged item

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a borrower who uses a borrowed item before pledging it is not liable if he later returns to compliance, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A borrower who uses an item before pledging it can be absolved by returning to compliance, unlike a borrower for benefit.

This passage from the Hidayah commentary addresses a nuanced scenario in pledge (rahn): when a borrower uses a borrowed item before pledging it, then later returns to compliance, is he liable for the unauthorised use? The Hanafi school holds he is not, treating him like a depositary. The Shafi'i school disagrees, imposing liability for any breach of trust. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main rulings
Locate the ruling on the pledgor's injury (compensable) and the pledgee's injury (falls from debt). Then focus on the specific scenario of the borrower's prior use.
The passage begins with general rules then moves to the borrower case.
2
Understand the borrower's scenario
A borrowed item (slave or animal) is used by the borrower before he pledges it. Later, he pledges it, repays the debt, but the item perishes in the pledgee's hands. The question: is the borrower liable for the prior unauthorised use?
Assume the use was without permission.
3
Grasp the Hanafi reasoning
The borrower is like a depositary (wadi'), not a regular borrower, because he borrowed for the purpose of pledging, not for benefit. A depositary who returns to compliance (i.e., acts properly) is absolved of liability for prior violations.
The hand of the depositary is like the owner's hand; return restores the owner's control legally.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that any unauthorised use is a violation of trust that creates liability, and mere return does not erase it.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In a Hanafi court, the borrower would not be liable; in a Shafi'i court, he would be required to compensate.
This affects transactions involving borrowed collateral.

Source Text

If he used it or rode it before [the pledge], and the pledgor's injury to the pledge is compensable, and the pledgee's injury to it falls from his debt; and if he used it or rode it before, because he was a trustee who violated then returned to compliance, so he does not guarantee, contrary to al-Shafi'i. [1] His statement: 'And if he used it or rode it before...' etc.; it is a conditional 'if'; i.e., if the borrowed item was a slave, and he used him or a mount and rode it before he pledged them, then he pledged them for a sum like their value, then he paid the money but did not take possession of them until they perished with the pledgee, then there is no liability on the pledgor; i.e., no liability for transgression, not no liability for repayment of debt; because the pledgor after paying the debt recoups what he paid; because when the pledge perished in the hands of the pledgee, he became one who satisfied his right from the property of the pledge, so the lender recovers from the pledgor what was used for satisfaction. Thus in Radd al-Muhtar. [2] His statement: 'then returned to compliance, so he does not guarantee'; but in al-Shurunbulali: from al-Imadiyya: the lessee or borrower, if they violate then return to compliance, they are not freed from liability according to the fatwa. He said in Radd al-Muhtar: This is about a lessee or borrower of something for benefit, but our case is about a borrower of something to pledge it, and he is like a depositary, not a borrower, as mentioned earlier, and the depositary is freed by return to compliance. And a distinction is made between them in al-Hidayah and its commentaries: because the hand of the borrower is his own hand, so by return he does not become a returner to the owner, neither in reality nor legally, unlike the depositary because his hand is like the owner's hand, so by return to compliance he becomes a returner to him legally. I say: similarly, the lessee's hand is his own hand because he holds the object for himself, not for its owner, so ponder. (3) His statement: 'on the pledge is compensable' because it is a destruction of a binding and respected right, and attachment of the like to the property.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage addresses the liability for damage to pledged property. It states that if the pledgor (الراهن) causes injury to the pledged item, it is compensable (i.e., must be paid for). If the pledgee (المرتهن) causes injury, the amount is deducted from the debt. This applies even if the borrower (المستعير) had previously used the pledged item (like riding a mount or employing a slave) before it was pledged; such prior unauthorized use does not create liability if he later returns to compliance (عاد إلى الوفاق), because he is considered a trustee (أمين) who violated trust but then rectified. This ruling differs from Imam al-Shafi'i, who would impose liability. The commentary elaborates with an example: if a person borrowed a slave or animal, used it, then pledged it for a loan, later repaid the loan, but the pledged item perished in the pledgee's hands before the borrower could take possession, then the borrower (who is the pledgor) is not liable for transgression; he only repays the debt and recovers from the lender? Actually careful: The commentary explains that the pledgor after paying the debt recovers from the lender (المعير) because the pledgee's possession was effective. However, the key point is about the borrower's return to compliance. The commentary also cites a difference from al-Shurunbulali: in the case of a lessee or borrower for benefit, return to compliance does not absolve liability, but the borrower here is like a depositary (مودع), whose return to compliance does absolve. Al-Hidayah distinguishes: the borrower's hand is his own, so returning does not legally restore the item to the owner, unlike the depositary whose hand is like the owner's. So the ruling is specific to the context of pledging a borrowed item.

Key Terms
جناية (jinayah): Injury or damage caused to the pledged property, whether by the pledgor or pledgee.
المستعير (al-musta'ir): The borrower of an item that is later pledged; in this context, he may become the pledgor.
الوفاق (al-wifaq): Compliance; returning to acting in accordance with the owner's permission.
أمين (amin): Trustee; one who holds property with permission and is not liable for loss without negligence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a borrower uses a borrowed slave before pledging him, but later returns to compliance by pledging him properly and then the slave perishes in the pledgee's hands?
A) The borrower is liable for the unauthorised use.
B) The borrower is not liable because he returned to compliance.
C) The borrower is liable only if the slave was damaged.
D) The borrower is liable regardless of return to compliance.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a borrower who uses a borrowed item before pledging it is absolved of liability if he returns to compliance, because his hand is akin to that of a depositary.

Liability of a Pawner Who Used the Pawn Before Pawning: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute about pawner's liability after returning to compliance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a pawner's liability for transgression after returning to compliance, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A pawner who violated trust by using the pawn before pawning is not liable for transgression if he later returns to compliance.

This lesson examines a dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding a pawner who used the pawn (e.g., rode a horse) before pawning it, then pawned it, paid the debt, but the pawn perished in the mortgagee's possession. The key question: does the initial violation make him permanently liable, or does returning to compliance restore his trustee status? The Hanafi school holds the latter, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds the former.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The pawner is not liable for transgression (ضمان التعدي) because he returned to compliance by pawning the item legitimately and paying the debt.
He remains liable for the debt (ضمان قضاء الدين) but that is a separate obligation.
2
Identify the opponent's view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the pawner remains liable for transgression because the initial violation makes him a guarantor (ضامن).
The Shafi'i school does not recognize the restorative effect of returning to compliance.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opposition argues that using the pawn without permission is a breach of trust that creates a permanent liability, regardless of subsequent actions.
This is based on the principle that a violator becomes a guarantor.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school distinguishes the pawner from a borrower for use: the pawner is like a depositary (مودع) whose trustee status is restored upon returning to compliance.
The hand of the pawner becomes like the mortgagee's hand after pawning, so returning to compliance is akin to returning the item to the owner.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafi – no liability for transgression; Shafi'i – liability remains. This affects compensation claims.
The debt repayment is wajib in both schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قوله : وإن استخدمه أو ركبه من قبل ... الخ ؛ إن وصلية ؛ أي بأن كان المستعار عبداً، فاستخدمه أو دابَّة فركبها قبل أن يرهنهما ، ثم رهنهما بمال مثل قيمتها، ثم قضى المال فلم يقبضهما حتى هلكا عند المرتهن ، فلا ضمان على الراهن ؛ أي ضمان التعدي لا ضمان قضاء الدين; لأنَّ الراهن بعدما قضى الدين يرجعُ بما أدى ; لأنَّ الرهنَ لَمَّا هلك في يد المرتهن صار مستوفياً حقه من ماليَّة الرهن ، فيرجعُ المعير على الراهن بما وقع به الإيفاء. هكذا في رد المحتار).
قوله : ثم عاد إلى الوفاق فلا يضمن ; لكن في «الشرنبلالي»: عــن «العمادية»: المستأجر أو المستعير إذا خالفا ثم عادا إلى الوفاق لا يبرأ عن الضمان على ما عليه الفتوى.
قال في رد المحتار) : هذا في المستأجر أو المستعير لشيء ينتفع به، وكلامنا في مستعير شيء ليرهنه ، وهو بمنزلة المودع لا المستعير، كما مرَّ آنفا، والمودع يبرأ بالعود إلى الوفاق.
وفرق بينهما في «الهداية» وشروحها : بأنّ يد المستعير يد نفسه، فلا يصير بالعود راداً على المالك لا حقيقة ولا حكماً، بخلاف المودع ; لأنَّ يده كيد المالك، فبالعود إلى الوفاق يصير راداً عليه حكماً ، قلت : وكذا المستأجر يده يد نفسه ; لأنه يمسك العين لنفسه لا بصاحبها، فليتأمل.
And if he used it or rode it before, and the injury of the pawner upon the pawn is guaranteed, and the injury of the mortgagee upon him drops from his debt, even if he used or rode it before, because he is a trustee who violated then returned to compliance, so he is not liable, contrary to al-Shafi'i. His statement: 'And if he used it or rode it before...' etc.; the 'in' is connected; meaning that if the borrowed item was a slave, and he used him, or an animal and he rode it before pawning them, then pawned them for a debt equal to their value, then paid off the debt but did not take possession of them until they perished with the mortgagee, then there is no liability on the pawner; meaning liability for transgression, not liability for repaying the debt; because the pawner, after paying the debt, recovers what he paid; because when the pawn perished in the mortgagee's hand, he became one who has satisfied his right from the value of the pawn, so the lender has recourse against the pawner for what was satisfied. This is in Radd al-Muhtar. His statement: 'Then he returned to compliance so he is not liable'; but in al-Shurunbulali: from al-Imadiyya: The lessee or borrower, if they violate then return to compliance, they are not absolved from liability according to the fatwa. He said in Radd al-Muhtar: This is for a lessee or borrower of something for benefit, but our case is about a borrower of something to pawn it, and he is like a depositary, not a borrower, as mentioned earlier, and a depositary is absolved by returning to compliance. And the difference between them is mentioned in al-Hidayah and its commentaries: because the hand of the borrower is his own hand, so by returning he does not become a returner to the owner either in reality or legally, unlike the depositary because his hand is like the owner's hand, so by returning to compliance he becomes a returner to him legally. I say: Similarly, the lessee's hand is his own hand because he holds the object for himself, not for its owner, so consider.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the liability of a pawner who had used the pawn (e.g., a slave or riding animal) before pawning it, then later pawns it, pays off the debt, but the pawn is destroyed in the mortgagee's possession before release. The Hanafi ruling: the pawner is not liable for transgression (ضمان التعدي) because he was a trustee (أمين) who had violated his trust by using the pawn without permission, but then he returned to compliance (عاد إلى الوفاق) by pawning it legitimately. The key is that the pawner's initial violation was temporary and he effectively returned the pawn to the mortgagee's trust. The Shafi'i position opposes, likely considering the initial violation as making him a guarantor permanently. The author then refines the ruling: the pawner is liable to repay the debt but not for transgression. The commentary clarifies that the pawner recovers from the mortgagee's estate because the pawn perished while securing the debt, so the mortgagee effectively satisfied his debt. A distinction is drawn between a borrower (مستعير) for use and a borrower for pawning: the latter is like a depositary (مودع), who is absolved upon returning to compliance, whereas a borrower for use remains liable even after returning. The reasoning in al-Hidayah is that the hand of the borrower is his own hand, so returning does not make him a returner to the owner legally. The author concludes with a note that the lessee (مستأجر) is similar.

Key Terms
الرهن (ar-rahn): The property given as collateral for a debt; the pawn.
الأمين (al-amin): A trustee; one entrusted with property without liability for loss except by transgression.
الوفاق (al-wifaq): Compliance; returning to the agreed terms of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the pawner is considered a guarantor initially.
B) Because the pawner becomes like a depositary upon returning to compliance.
C) Because the pawner's debt extinguishes the liability.
D) Because the mortgagee assumed all risk.

Key Takeaway
A pawner who violates trust by using the pawn before pawning is not liable for transgression if he returns to compliance, because his hand becomes like the mortgagee's hand, similar to a depositary.

Pawn's Injury to Mortgagee: Dropping vs. Considering
Explaining intra-Hanafi dispute on pawn's injury to mortgagee.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position and the Two Companions' view on a pawned slave's injury to the mortgagee, explain the thamarah al-khilaf, and apply the condition that compensation drops only for monetary debts.

Core Idea
An injury by the pawn on the mortgagee either drops from the debt (Abu Hanifa) or allows cancellation (Two Companions).

When a pawned slave injures the pawner or mortgagee, the Hanafi school has a nuanced ruling. This lesson explores the key disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, on whether the mortgagee can claim compensation for the injury or must accept it as a reduction of the debt. The passage also clarifies when the compensation is guaranteed and when it drops.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the injury
The pawned slave (pawn) injures either the pawner (owner) or the mortgagee (creditor). The ruling differs based on the victim.
Injury here means tort (جناية) causing financial loss.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling
Abu Hanifa rules that injury on the pawner is guaranteed (مضمونة) – the mortgagee must compensate. Injury on the mortgagee drops (هدر) from the debt – no separate compensation.
The mortgagee has an obligation to clear the slave (تخليص) from the injury; giving him both debt and compensation is contradictory.
3
State the Two Companions' ruling
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that injury on the mortgagee is considered (معتبرة). The mortgagee can cancel the pawn and take the slave as compensation, or leave it if he wishes.
They analogize the mortgagee to a third party since the injury occurred on a non-owner.
4
Examine the proofs (talil)
Abu Hanifa: the injury occurred in the mortgagee's guarantee; he must clear it, so imposing both debt and compensation is unjust. The Two Companions: the injury happened on a non-owner, so it's like injury to a stranger; considering it gives a practical benefit (handing over the slave).
The author in al-Hidayah supports Abu Hanifa's view as mufta bihi.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf and nuances
Practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa, the mortgagee's debt reduces by the value of the injury. Under the Two Companions, the mortgagee can cancel the pawn. Also, the compensation drops only if the debt is monetary (dirhams/dinars); if it is kind (measured/weighed), it does not drop. If the pawn's value exceeds the debt, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa.
This nuance is important for fatwa application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : على الرهن مضمونة ; لأنه تفويت حق لازم محترم، وتعلق مثلِهِ بالمال بقدرها، وجناية الرهن عليهما، وعلى مالهما هدر هذا عند أبي حنيفة ، وقالا : جناية الرهن على المرتهن معتبرة ; لأنها حصلت على غير مالكه ، وفي الاعتبار فائدة : وهي الدفع بالجناية إلى المرتهن، فإن شاءَ الرَّاهِنُ والمرتهن أبطلا الرهن ودفع بالجناية إلى المرتهن، فإن قال المرتهن : لا أطلب الجناية، فهو رهن على حاله، وله : إن الجناية حصلت في ضمان المرتهن، فعليه تخليصه فلا يفيد وجوب الضمان له مع وجوب التخليص عليه.
يجعل المالك كالأجنبي في حق الضمان كتعلق حق الورثة بمال المريض مرض الموت بمنع نفاذ تبرعه فيما وراء الثلث، والعبد الموصى بخدمته إذا أتلفه الورثة ضمنوا قيمته ; ليشتري بها عبداً يقوم مقامه. هكذا في «الهداية».
[ ۱ ] قوله : من دينه بقدرها ; معناه أن يكون الضمان على صفة الدين، بأن يكون الدين دراهم أو دنانير، أما إذا كان الدين مكيلاً أو موزوناً فلا يسقط ، وهذا لأنّ العينَ ملك المالك، وقد تعدى عليه المرتهن، فيضمنه لمالكه.

[٢] قوله : وله ; في «الهداية» : إن هذه الجناية لو اعتبرناها للمرتهن كان عليه التطهير عن الجناية ; لأنها حصلت في ضمانه ، فلا يفيد وجوب الضمان له مع وجوب التخليص عليه، وجنايته على مال المرتهن لا تعتبر بالاتفاق إذا كانت قيمته والدين سواء ; لأنه لا فائدة في اعتبارها ; لأنه لا يتملك العبد ، وإن كانت القيمة أكثر من الدين فعن أبي حنيفة له إنه يعتبر بقدر الأمانة ; لأنّ الفضل ليس في ضمانه، فأشبه جناية العبد الوديعة على المستودع، وعنه أنها لا تعتبر; لأن حكم الرهن وهو الحبس فيه ثابت فصار كالمضمون وهذا بخلاف جناية الرهن على رهن الراهن، أو من المرتهن ; لأنّ الأملاك حقيقة متباينة، فصار كالجناية على الأجنبي.
His statement: upon the pawn is guaranteed because it is a removal of a necessary and sacred right, and attachment of the like to the property according to its extent, and the injury of the pawn upon them both and upon their property is disregarded. This according to Abu Hanifa. And they (the two companions) said: The injury of the pawn upon the mortgagee is considered because it occurred upon someone other than its owner, and in consideration there is a benefit: namely, handing over the injury to the mortgagee. So if the pawner and mortgagee wish, they cancel the pawn and hand over the injury to the mortgagee. And if the mortgagee says: I do not claim the injury, then it remains a pawn as is. And he (Abu Hanifa) has that the injury occurred under the guarantee of the mortgagee, so it is upon him to clear it, so establishing liability for him along with the obligation to clear does not benefit. He makes the owner like a stranger regarding the right of guarantee, similar to the attachment of the right of heirs to the property of a person terminally ill preventing the execution of his gift beyond one-third, and a slave bequeathed for his service if the heirs destroy him, they guarantee his value to buy a slave to take his place. This is in al-Hidayah. [1] His statement: from his debt according to its extent means that the guarantee is of the same type as the debt, meaning the debt is dirhams or dinars; but if the debt is measured or weighed, then it does not drop. And this is because the object is the property of the owner, and the mortgagee has transgressed upon him, so he guarantees it to its owner. And this is the benefit. [2] His statement: And he has; in al-Hidayah: If we were to consider this injury for the mortgagee, he would have to purify himself from the injury because it occurred in his guarantee, so establishing liability for him along with the obligation to clear does not benefit. And his injury upon the property of the mortgagee is not considered by agreement if its value and the debt are equal; because there is no benefit in considering it because he does not own the slave. And if the value is greater than the debt, then from Abu Hanifa there is that he considers it to the extent of the trust (amanah) because the surplus is not in his guarantee, so it resembles the injury of a deposited slave upon the depositary; and from him that it is not considered because the rule of pawn, which is detention, is established, so it becomes like a guaranteed thing. And this is unlike the injury of the pawn upon the pawn of the pawner, or from the mortgagee, because the properties are truly distinct, so it becomes like injury upon a stranger.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling when a pawned slave commits an injury (janiya) against the pawner or the mortgagee. Abu Hanifa's position: the injury upon the pawner is guaranteed (مضمونة), meaning the pawner is entitled to compensation from the mortgagee because the pawn is in mortgagee's custody; the injury upon the mortgagee is dropped from his debt (يسقط من دينه) because the pawn is in his guarantee. The Two Companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the injury upon the mortgagee is considered (معتبرة), giving the mortgagee the option to either cancel the pawn and take the slave as compensation for the injury, or leave the pawn as is. Abu Hanifa's proof: the injury occurred while the pawn was under the mortgagee's guarantee; therefore, the mortgagee is obliged to clear the pawn from the injury, and considering the injury for his benefit would give him both the debt and the compensation, which is contradictory. The author then clarifies that the compensation drops only if the debt is monetary; if it is kind (e.g., wheat), it does not drop because the injury is assessed in value. Finally, a nuance: if the pawn's value exceeds the debt, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa about whether the injury is considered for the surplus; the default is that it is not considered because the pawn's status as collateral prevents ownership. This differs from a deposited slave injuring the depositary, where the surplus is considered.

Key Terms
الجناية (al-janiya): An injury or tort committed by the pawn (e.g., a slave) against a person or property.
المضمونة (al-mamduna): Guaranteed; the injury is compensable.
المعتبرة (al-mu'tabara): Considered; the injury has legal effect, allowing cancellation of the pawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens when a pawned slave injures the mortgagee?
A) The mortgagee can cancel the pawn and take the slave as compensation.
B) The value of the injury drops from the mortgagee's debt.
C) The pawner must compensate the mortgagee separately.
D) The pawn is invalidated and the slave is freed.

Key Takeaway
For pawned property injuries, the Hanafi mufta bihi is that injury on the mortgagee reduces the debt, not a separate claim.

Jinaayah of the Pawned Slave on the Pledgee's Property: Abu Hanifah vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether injury by pawned slave to pledgee's property is valid and its effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on injury by a pawned slave to the pledgee's property and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
An injury under guarantee cannot generate a claim; the pledgee cannot both guarantee and collect damages.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: if a pawned slave injures the property of the pledgee (murtahin), does the pledgee have a right to compensation? Imam Abu Hanifah and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagree. Abu Hanifah argues that the injury is null because it occurred under the pledgee's own guarantee, while the Sahibayn see it as a valid claim because the injury was on non-owner property. Let's unpack the reasoning and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
What is the act and the legal question? The jinaayah of the pawned slave on the pledgee's property – is it considered legally valid (i.e., does it give a right to damages)?
The phrase 'هذا عند أبي حنيفة' sets the baseline.
2
State Abu Hanifah's position and proof
Abu Hanifah says the injury is not considered (hader). His proof: the injury occurred under the pledgee's guarantee (daman), so the pledgee must extricate the slave; he cannot both guarantee and claim.
He uses analogies from heirs' rights in marad al-mawt and a bequeathed slave.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
The Sahibayn say the injury is considered (mu'tabarah). Their proof: the injury was on property of a non-owner (the pledgee is not the owner), so considering it provides benefit – the pledgee can either claim damages or nullify the pledge.
They focus on the benefit of giving the pledgee a legal option.
4
Analyse Abu Hanifah's response
Abu Hanifah objects: the pledgee cannot have both guarantee and claim. The owner is treated as a stranger regarding guarantee, similar to the heirs' right in marad al-mawt preventing the patient's gift beyond one-third, and the bequeathed slave case where heirs must pay value if they destroy the slave.
These analogies show that a pre-existing right (guarantee) bars a claim.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifah, the pledgee cannot claim damages; under the Sahibayn, he can claim or nullify the pledge. The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifah's, as stated in al-Hidayah.
Within Abu Hanifah's position, there are two narrations when the slave's value exceeds the debt, but the mufta bihi is the absolute non-consideration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بقدرها، وجناية الرهن عليهما، وعلى مالهما هدر)، هذا عند أبي حنيفة ، وقالا : جناية الرهن على المرتهن معتبرة ؛ لأنها حصلت على غير مالكه ، وفي الاعتبار فائدة : وهي الدفع بالجناية إلى المرتهن، فإن شاءَ الرَّاهِنُ والمرتهن أبطلا الرهن ودفع بالجناية إلى المرتهن، فإن قال المرتهن : لا أطلب الجناية، فهو رهن على حاله، وله : إن الجناية حصلت في ضمان المرتهن، فعليه تخليصه فلا يفيد وجوب الضمان له مع وجوب التخليص عليه. يجعل المالك كالأجنبي في حق الضمان كتعلق حق الورثة بمال المريض مرض الموت بمنع نفاذ تبرعه فيما وراء الثلث، والعبد الموصى بخدمته إذا أتلفه الورثة ضمنوا قيمته ؛ ليشتري بها عبداً يقوم مقامه. هكذا في «الهداية»(۱). [ ۱ ] قوله : من دينه بقدرها ؛ معناه أن يكون الضمان على صفة الدين، بأن يكون الدين دراهم أو دنانير، أما إذا كان الدين مكيلاً أو موزوناً فلا يسقط ، وهذا لأنّ العينَ ملك المالك، وقد تعدى عليه المرتهن، فيضمنه لمالكه. [٢] قوله : وله ؛ في «الهداية» (۲) : إن هذه الجناية لو اعتبرناها للمرتهن كان عليه التطهير عن الجناية ؛ لأنها حصلت في ضمانه ، فلا يفيد وجوب الضمان له مع وجوب التخليص عليه، وجنايته على مال المرتهن لا تعتبر بالاتفاق إذا كانت قيمته والدين سواء ؛ لأنه لا فائدة في اعتبارها ؛ لأنه لا يتملك العبد ، وإن كانت القيمة أكثر من الدين فعن أبي حنيفة له إنه يعتبر بقدر الأمانة ؛ لأنّ الفضل ليس في ضمانه، فأشبه جناية العبد الوديعة على المستودع، وعنه أنها لا تعتبر؛ لأن حكم الرهن وهو الحبس فيه ثابت فصار كالمضمون وهذا بخلاف جناية الرهن على رهن الراهن، أو من المرتهن ؛ لأنّ الأملاك حقيقة متباينة، فصار كالجناية على الأجنبي.
To its extent, and the injury of the pawn [slave] upon both [the pawner and pledgee] and upon their property is wasted. This is according to Abu Hanifah. The two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said: The injury of the pawn upon the pledgee is considered valid because it occurred upon other than the owner [i.e., the pledgee is not the owner], and in consideration there is a benefit: which is the payment by the injury to the pledgee. If the pawner and the pledgee wish, they may nullify the pledge and pay by the injury to the pledgee. If the pledgee says: I do not claim the injury, then it remains a pledge as it was. And for him [Abu Hanifah]: The injury occurred under the guarantee of the pledgee, so upon him is to extricate it, so the obligation of guarantee to him does not benefit with the obligation of extrication upon him. The owner is made like a stranger regarding guarantee, like the attachment of the heirs' right to the property of the patient in death illness preventing the effectiveness of his gratuitous gift beyond the third, and the slave bequeathed his service if the heirs destroy him, they guarantee his price to buy a slave to take his place. Thus in al-Hidayah (1). [1] His saying: from his debt to its extent; its meaning is that the guarantee is upon the description of the debt, whether the debt is dirhams or dinars. But if the debt is measured or weighed, it does not fall. And this is because the specific property is owned by the owner, and the pledgee has transgressed upon it, so he guarantees it to its owner. [2] His saying: and for him; in al-Hidayah (2): If this injury were considered for the pledgee, he would be obligated to purify from the injury because it occurred under his guarantee; so the obligation of guarantee does not benefit him with the obligation of extrication upon him. And his injury upon the property of the pledgee is not considered by agreement if its value and the debt are equal, because there is no benefit in considering it, because he does not own the slave. If the value is more than the debt, then from Abu Hanifah there is a narration that it is considered to the extent of the trust, because the excess is not under his guarantee, so it resembles the injury of a slave in trust (wadi'ah) upon the depository; and from him that it is not considered because the ruling of pledge – which is detention – is established in it, so it becomes like guaranteed. And this differs from the injury of the pawn upon the pawn of the pawner, or from the pledgee, because the ownerships are truly distinct, so it becomes like injury upon a stranger.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifah and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the legal status of an injury (jinaayah) caused by a pawned slave to the property of the pledgee (murtahin). According to Abu Hanifah, such an injury is not considered valid (i.e., no liability arises) because it occurred while the slave was under the guarantee (daman) of the pledgee. Since the pledgee is responsible for the slave's safety, he must extricate the slave from the injury; thus, recognizing a claim for damages would be contradictory. The two Sahibayn argue that the injury should be considered valid because the slave committed the injury on the property of someone other than its owner (the pledgee is not the owner), and this provides a benefit: the pledgee can claim damages from the pawner or nullify the pledge. Abu Hanifah's position is supported by analogies: such as the right of heirs over a patient's property in death illness, or a slave bequeathed for service whose destruction obliges the heirs to pay compensation. The commentary from al-Hidayah further clarifies that the injury is only relevant if it exceeds the debt. Abu Hanifah has two narrations when the slave's value exceeds the debt: one considers the injury to the extent of the trust (amanah), the other does not consider it at all. The latter view is analogized to a slave in trust. This ruling differs when the injury is upon the pawner's other property or upon the pledgee's property, where the matter is treated as injury upon a stranger due to distinct ownerships.

Key Terms
جناية (jinaayah): An injury or tort committed by the pawned slave upon the property of the pledgee or others.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability; the pledgee is responsible for the pawned item and must extricate it from injury.
مرتهن (murtahin): The pledgee; the person who receives the pawned item as security for a debt.
راهن (rahin): The pawner; the person who gives the pawned item as security.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the position of Imam Abu Hanifah regarding an injury caused by a pawned slave to the property of the pledgee?
A) The injury is considered valid and the pledgee can claim damages.
B) The injury is not considered valid because it occurred under the pledgee's guarantee.
C) The injury is considered valid only if the value of the slave exceeds the debt.
D) The pledgee must nullify the pledge and pay damages to the pawner.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, if a pawned slave injures the pledgee's property, the injury is not considered valid because the pledgee's guarantee of the pawn prevents him from claiming damages.

Effect of Decrease in Pawn Value on Debt
Rulings when pawned slave's value decreases, then killed or sold, and the debt is paid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of market price decrease on a pawned item and explain why the debt remains, distinguishing the majority view from Zufar's.

Core Idea
A drop in market value does not cancel a pawn debt; only physical destruction matters.

A common concern in pawn transactions is whether a drop in the item's market value reduces the debt. This lesson examines a specific case from al-Hidayah where a pawned slave's value plummets, and then the slave is either killed or sold. The Hanafi school holds that the debt remains intact; only physical loss or authorized sale alters the pledgee's claim. We will explore the reasoning behind this position and the intra-school disagreement with Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? A pawned slave whose value decreases. The ruling is that the debt is not reduced; the pledgee collects the substitute (blood money or sale price) and the remainder of the debt falls.
This is a case ruling, not a general obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The text does not cite a specific verse or hadith but relies on reasoning: decrease in price does not cancel debt because it is not destruction. The pledgee's hand is one of execution (yad al-istifa'), so he collects from the substitute.
The proof is based on the nature of the pledgee's possession and the distinction between price and substance.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does the proof lead to the ruling? The pledgee's hand is for execution, meaning he can take the pawn's value. When the pawn is destroyed, the substitute (blood money) stands in place of the property, so the pledgee takes it. Price decrease does not affect entitlement because it is not a permanent loss.
Zufar's analogy to physical decrease is rejected because price can recover.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Who disagrees? Imam Zufar argues that price decrease should cancel debt like a decrease in substance, based on qiyas.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which position is relied upon? The majority Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is that price decrease does not cancel debt. The commentary explicitly rejects Zufar's view.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.

[٢] (ومن رهن عبداً يعدلُ ألفاً بألف مؤجل فصارت قيمته مئة فقتله رجل، وغرم مئة، وحلّ أجلُهُ قبض مرتهنه المئة من حقه وسقط باقيه) ؛ لأن نقصان السعر لا يوجب سقوط الدِّينِ عندنا، خلافاً لزفر ، فإذا كان الدين باقياً، ويد المرتهن يد الاستيفاء فيصيرُ مستوفياً للكلِّ من الابتداء. ( وإن باعه بأمره ) ، وقبض ثمنه رجع بما بقي) : أي إن باعَهُ المرتهن بأمرِ الراهن بالمئة، بعد أن صار قيمته مئة ، وقبض ثمنه، رجع بما بقي ؛ لأنَّ الدِّينَ لم يسقط بنقصان السعر ؛ لأن نقصان السعر ليس هلاكاً ؛ لاحتمال العود على ما [ ١ ] قوله : لأن نقصان السعر ... الخ ؛ توضيحه : أنّ نقصان السعر عبارة عن فتور رغبات الناس، وذلك لا يعتبرُ في البيع حتى لا يثبت به الخيار، ولا في الغصب حتى لا يجب الضمان بخلافِ نقصان العين ؛ لأنّ بفواتِ جزء منه يتقرر الاستيفاء فيه، إذ يدُ المرتهن يد الاستيفاء. وإذا لم يسقط شيء من الدين بنقصان السعر بقي مرهوناً بكل الدين، فإذا قتله حرٌ غَرمَ قيمته مئة ؛ لأنه تعتبر قيمته يوم الإتلاف في ضمان الإتلاف ؛ لأن الجابر بقدر الفائت، وأخذه المرتهن ؛ لأنه بدل الماليَّة في حق المستحق، وإن كان مقابلا بالدم على أصلنا حتى لا يزداد على دِيَةِ الحرّ ؛ لأنَّ المولى استحقه : بسبب المالية، وحق المرتهن متعلّق بالمالية، فكذا فيما قام مقامه ، ثم لا يرجع على الراهن بشيء ؛ لأنّ يد الرهن يد الاستيفاء من الابتداء. [٢]قوله : خلافاً لزفر له ؛ هو يقول : إنّ المالية قد انتقصت، فأشبه انتقاص العين. [٣] قوله : وإن باعه بأمره.... الخ ؛ صورته : إنّ المرتهن باع العبد المرهون الذي تراجع قيمته إلى النقصان، وقبض ثمنه قضاءً من حقه رجع بما بقي من الدين ؛ لأنَّ المرتهن إذا باعه بإذن الراهن صار كأنَّ الراهن استرده وباعه بنفسه، ولو كان كذلك يبطل، ويبقى الدين إلا بقدر ما استوفى كذا هذا.
And whoever pawns a slave worth a thousand [dirhams] for a deferred debt of a thousand, then its value becomes a hundred, then a man kills him, and pays a hundred [as blood money], and his term arrives, his pledgee takes the hundred from his right and the remainder falls. And if he [the pledgee] sells it by his [the pawner's] order, and takes its price, he returns to what remains. [3] [2] (And whoever pawns a slave worth a thousand for a deferred debt of a thousand, then its value becomes a hundred, then a man kills him, and pays a hundred, and his term arrives, his pledgee takes the hundred from his right and the remainder falls) because decrease in price does not cause cancellation of the debt according to us, contrary to Zufar. So when the debt remains, and the hand of the pledgee is the hand of execution, then he becomes a collector of the whole from the beginning. (And if he sells it by his order, and takes its price, he returns to what remains): meaning if the pledgee sells it by the pawner's order for a hundred, after its value became a hundred, and takes its price, he returns to what remains because the debt did not fall due to decrease in price, because decrease in price is not destruction, due to the possibility of return. [1] His saying: because decrease in price... etc.; its clarification: that decrease in price is an expression of the weakness of people's desires, and that is not considered in sale so that option is not established by it, nor in usurpation so that guarantee is not obligated, unlike decrease in the substance of the item, because by the loss of a part of it the execution is established in it, for the hand of the pledgee is the hand of execution. And if nothing of the debt falls due to decrease in price, it remains pawned for all the debt. So if a free man kills him, he pays its value of a hundred because its value on the day of destruction is considered in the guarantee of destruction because the compensator is to the extent of the lost. And the pledgee takes it because it is the substitute for the property in the right of the entitled, even though it is appraised against blood according to our principle, so that it does not exceed the blood money of a free man, because the owner deserves it due to property, and the right of the pledgee pertains to property, so similarly for what stands in its place. Then he does not seek recourse against the pawner for anything because the hand of the pawn is the hand of execution from the beginning. [2] His saying: contrary to Zufar; he says: that the property has decreased, so it resembles decrease of the substance. [3] His saying: And if he sells it by his order... etc.; its scenario: The pledgee sold the pawned slave whose value had declined, and took its price as payment from his right, then he returns to what remains of the debt because when the pledgee sells with the permission of the pawner, it becomes as if the pawner took it back and sold it himself. And if that were the case, it would be null, and the debt remains except to the extent of what was collected, like this.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage provides rulings for a specific scenario in pawnage (rahn): a slave is pawned for a deferred debt of 1000, but its market value drops to 100. Two sub-scenarios are discussed. First, if a free man kills the slave and pays blood money (ghurm) of 100, the pledgee collects this 100 from his due, and the remaining debt falls (sakat baqeeh). The reasoning is that a decrease in market price (nuqsan al-si'r) does not cause the debt to be cancelled according to the Hanafi school, contrary to Imam Zufar who compares it to a decrease in the substance of the item (nuqsan al-'ayn). The pledgee's hand is one of execution (yad al-istifa'), so he becomes as if he collected the entire debt from the beginning. Consequently, the blood money replaces the property value, and the pledgee takes it. Second, if the pledgee sells the slave with the pawner's permission for 100, he collects the price and returns to what remains of the debt. This is because the sale with permission is like the pawner taking back the pawn and selling it himself, so the debt remains except for what was paid. The commentary clarifies that decrease in price is not considered in sale or usurpation; only physical decrease matters. Thus, the key principle is that market fluctuation does not affect the debt or the pawn's status.

Key Terms
نقصان السعر (nuqsan al-si'r): Decrease in market price or value without any physical damage to the pawned item.
يد الاستيفاء (yad al-istifa'): The hand of execution; the pledgee's possession is for collecting the debt, like a trustee for the debt.
غرم (ghurm): Blood money or financial compensation paid by a killer for taking a life; here it is the value of the slave paid by the free killer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in the text, why does a decrease in market price of a pawned item not cancel any part of the debt?
A) Because the pawner must give permission for the debt to be reduced.
B) Because price decrease is not considered destruction due to the possibility of recovery.
C) Because the pledgee automatically loses his right if the value drops.
D) Because the debt is secured by the pawner's other property.

Key Takeaway
Market price fluctuations do not cancel a pawn debt; only physical destruction or authorized sale with collection affects the pledgee's claim.

Effect of Decrease in Pawned Item's Value on Debt
Ruling on pawned item's market value decrease and killing by a free man

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that decrease in market value does not reduce the debt and analyze Zufar's opposing view within the school.

Core Idea
Market price drop never reduces the pawn debt; only physical loss can.

Imagine you pawn an item worth $1000 for a loan of $1000. If the item's market price drops to $100, does your debt drop? According to the Hanafi school, no — because a decrease in price is not a decrease in substance. This lesson unpacks that ruling through a famous intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar, and applies it to scenarios where the pawn is destroyed or sold.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the debt remains unchanged despite a drop in market value of the pawn. The mortgagee's hand is considered a hand of satisfaction (yad al-istifa), so he is deemed to have collected the entire debt from the beginning.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Zufar, a Hanafi imam, holds that the debt should be reduced proportionally to the decrease in value, analogous to physical loss.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The decrease in price (naqs al-sa'r) is not destruction; it is a mere fluctuation of people's desires. It does not remove any part of the pawn's substance, so the mortgagee's right remains attached to the entire original value.
Refer to the concept of yad al-istifa.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Zufar, the pawner could redeem the pawn by paying only the reduced value. Under the majority, the debt is fixed; if the pawn is destroyed and compensation paid, the mortgagee collects the entire debt from the compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن رهن عبداً يعدلُ ألفاً بألف مؤجل فصارت قيمته مئة فقتله رجل، وغَرِمَ مئة ، وحل أجله قبض مرتهنه المئة من حقه وسقط باقيه، وإن باعه بأمره، وقبض ثمنه رجع بما بقى

[٢] (ومن رهن عبداً يعدلُ ألفاً بألف مؤجل فصارت قيمته مئة فقتله رجل، وغرم مئة، وحلّ أجلُهُ قبض مرتهنه المئة من حقه وسقط باقيه) ؛ لأن نقصان السعر لا يوجب سقوط الدِّينِ عندنا، خلافاً لزفر ، فإذا كان الدين باقياً، ويد المرتهن يد الاستيفاء فيصيرُ مستوفياً للكلِّ من الابتداء. ( وإن باعه بأمره ) ، وقبض ثمنه رجع بما بقي) : أي إن باعَهُ المرتهن بأمرِ الراهن بالمئة، بعد أن صار قيمته مئة ، وقبض ثمنه، رجع بما بقي ؛ لأنَّ الدِّينَ لم يسقط بنقصان السعر ؛ لأن نقصان السعر ليس هلاكاً ؛ لاحتمال العود على ما [ ١ ] قوله : لأن نقصان السعر ... الخ ؛ توضيحه : أنّ نقصان السعر عبارة عن فتور رغبات الناس، وذلك لا يعتبرُ في البيع حتى لا يثبت به الخيار، ولا في الغصب حتى لا يجب الضمان بخلافِ نقصان العين ؛ لأنّ بفواتِ جزء منه يتقرر الاستيفاء فيه، إذ يدُ المرتهن يد الاستيفاء.
وإذا لم يسقط شيء من الدين بنقصان السعر بقي مرهوناً بكل الدين، فإذا قتله حرٌ غَرمَ قيمته مئة ؛ لأنه تعتبر قيمته يوم الإتلاف في ضمان الإتلاف ؛ لأن الجابر بقدر الفائت، وأخذه المرتهن ؛ لأنه بدل الماليَّة في حق المستحق، وإن كان مقابلا بالدم على أصلنا حتى لا يزداد على دِيَةِ الحرّ ؛ لأنَّ المولى استحقه : بسبب المالية، وحق المرتهن متعلّق بالمالية، فكذا فيما قام مقامه ، ثم لا يرجع على الراهن بشيء ؛ لأنّ يد الرهن يد الاستيفاء من الابتداء.
And if one pawns a slave worth a thousand for a deferred debt of a thousand, then his value becomes one hundred, and then a man kills him, and pays a hundred as compensation, and the debt matures, the mortgagee receives the hundred from his right and the remaining debt falls. And if he (the mortgagee) sells it by his (the pawner's) order and collects the price, he recovers what remains. ([The text] 'And if one pawns a slave...') Because the decrease in price does not necessitate the fall of the debt according to us, contrary to Zufar. So when the debt remains, and the hand of the mortgagee is a hand of satisfaction, so he becomes one who has collected the entirety from the beginning. (And if he sells it by his order and collects the price, he recovers what remains): Meaning if the mortgagee sells it by the order of the pawner for one hundred, after its value became one hundred, and he collects the price, he recovers what remains, because the debt did not fall due to the decrease in price, because the decrease in price is not destruction, because of the possibility of return... (clarification): That the decrease in price is a slackening of people's desires, and that is not considered in sale such that option is established by it, nor in usurpation such that guarantee becomes obligatory, unlike the decrease of the substance (physical loss); because by the loss of a part of it, satisfaction is effected therein, because the hand of the mortgagee is a hand of satisfaction. And if nothing of the debt fell by the decrease in price, it remains pawned for the entire debt. So if a free man kills him, he pays its value of one hundred; because its value on the day of destruction is considered in the guarantee for destruction, because the compensation is by the amount of the loss; and the mortgagee takes it, because it is a monetary substitute in respect of the entitled party, although it is compared to blood money according to our principle so that it does not exceed the blood money of a free man; because the master acquired it due to its monetary value, and the right of the mortgagee is attached to the monetary value, thus similarly what stands in its place. Then he does not recourse against the pawner for anything, because the hand of the pawn is a hand of satisfaction from the beginning.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage discusses a classic Hanafi scenario: a pawned item's market value drops drastically, but the debt remains unchanged because the decrease is in price, not in substance. The text then presents a case where the pawn is destroyed (killed by a free man) and the mortgagee receives compensation. According to the Hanafi school, because the mortgagee's hand is considered a hand of satisfaction (يد الاستيفاء), receiving the compensation of 100 satisfies the entire debt of 1000, and the remaining 900 is considered to have been collected from the beginning. This is contrary to Zufar, who would have reduced the debt proportionally. The text then adds a sub-case: if the mortgagee sells the pawn by the pawner's order after the price drop, collecting only 100, the remaining debt is not discharged; the mortgagee can recover the balance from the pawner. The reasoning is that sale does not constitute the same kind of satisfaction as destruction; the pawner's order implies he is responsible for the shortfall. The Hanafi position is that decrease in market value (نقصان السعر) is not like physical decrease (نقصان العين); it is only a change in people's desires and does not affect the validity of the pawn or the debt.

Key Terms
نقصان السعر (naqsān al-saʿr): Decrease in the market price of the pawned item, as opposed to physical loss.
يد الاستيفاء (yad al-istīfāʾ): The legal hand of satisfaction; the mortgagee's possession is deemed to be collecting the debt.
مرتهن (murtahin): The mortgagee (creditor) who receives the pawn.
راهن (rāhin): The pawner (debtor) who gives the pawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The debt remains unchanged.
C) The pawn becomes void.
D) The mortgagee must return the surplus.

Key Takeaway
Decrease in market price of a pawned item does not reduce the debt; only physical loss can affect the pawn's security function.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Pawned Slave Killed – Substitute and Option
Intra-Hanafi dispute on substitute slave compensating for killed pawn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar regarding the effect of a substitute slave given for a killed pawn, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When a pawned slave is killed, the substitute slave's treatment differs: full debt discharge (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf), option (Muhammad), or partial pawn (Zufar).

In Hanafi fiqh, when a pawned item is destroyed, the ruling often depends on whether the substitute is considered equivalent to the original. This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a pawned slave killed by another slave worth 100. The killer slave is given as compensation. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule that this fully redeems the pawn (فك بكل دينه), while Muhammad grants the pawner an option, and Zufar treats the substitute as a new pawn for only 100. We will explore the proofs and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the positions of the three Hanafi authorities
Read the text to extract the rulings of Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar. Note the exact wording: for the majority, 'فك بكل دينه'; for Muhammad, 'بالخيار'; for Zufar, 'يصير رهناً بمئة'.
2
Analyze the proof of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (قيام مقام)
They argue that the substitute stands in the place of the original in every respect – form and meaning – so it is as if the original remained and its value returned. This negates any change that would grant an option.
The commentary in the text stresses that the substitute is equivalent in humanity and legal standing.
3
Analyze the proof of Muhammad (qiyas on sold item killed before delivery)
Muhammad analogizes to a sold item that is killed before delivery: the buyer gets an option because the item has changed. Here, the pawn has changed (died), so the pawner should have an option.
The text notes that the qiyas is rejected by the majority because the change is not manifest (لم يظهر) due to the substitute's equivalence.
4
Analyze the proof of Zufar (partial pawn)
Zufar holds that the substitute only secures its own value (100), so the debt remains for the remaining amount. This is because he sees the substitute as a new pawn, not a full replacement.
The majority rebuts that the second slave stands fully in the place of the first, as per the principle of qiyām maqām.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The text indicates that the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position. This is also supported by later Hanafi authorities.
The dispute is legitimate ikhtilaf, but for fatwa, the majority position is preferred.

وإن قتله عبد يعدل مئة فدفع به فك بكل دينه كان، وإذا كان الدِّينُ باقياً، وقد أمرَ الرَّاهِنُ أن يبيعه بمئة يكونُ الباقي في ذمته. (وإن قتله عبد يعدل مئة فدفع به فك بكل دينه) (۱) ، هذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ، وعند محمد : هو بالخيار إن شاء فكه ، وإن شاءَ سَلَّمَ العبد المدفوع إلى المرتهن بماله وعند زفرَ الله : يصير رهناً بمئة ؛ لأنه بقي الخلف بقدر العُشر، فيبقى الدين بقدره. قلنا لزفر الله : إنَّ العبد الثاني قائم مقامَ الأَوَّلِ فصار كما كان الأوَّلُ قائماً"، وتراجع سعره. ثم لمحمد : أن المرهونَ تغيّر في ضمان المرتهن، فيخيرُ الرَّاهِنُ كالمبيع إذا قتل قبل القبض ، ولهما : أنّ التغير لم يظهر في حق العبد لقيام الثاني مقامه ] ١ ] قوله : فك ؛ أي خلص الرهن بأداء كلّ دينه. [۲]قوله : قائماً ؛ مقام الأول صورة ومعنى، أما صورة فظاهر، وأما معنى فلان القاتل كالمقتول في الآدمية والشرع اعتبره حراً من حيث الآدمية دون المالية، ألا ترى إلى استوائهما في حق القصاص، فكذا في حق الدفع. كذا في «العناية). (٤) قوله : لقيام الثاني مقامه ؛ كما ذكرناه آنفاً، وعين الرهن أمانة عند المرتهن عندنا، فلا يجوز تمليكه منه بغير رضاه ؛ ولأنّ جعل الرهن بالدين حكم جاهلي، وهو منسوخ بخلاف البيع ؛ لأنّ الخيار فيه حكمه الفسخ، وهو مشروع، وبخلاف الغصب ؛ لأن تملكه بأداء الضمان مشروع.
(۱) أي دفع العبد الجاني مقام العبد المقتول بسبب قتله افتكه الراهن بكل دينه ؛ لقيام الثاني مقام الأول لحما ودما. ينظر : (الدر المنتقى»(۲) : ٦٠٩).
(۲) «العناية» (۱۰ : ۱۹۱). (۳) (الكفاية» (۹: ١٢٤ - ١٢٥).
And if a slave worth one hundred kills him (the pawned slave), and (the killer) is given (as compensation), he redeems (the pawn) with all his debt. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad, he has the option: if he wishes he redeems it, and if he wishes he hands over the given slave to the mortgagee for (the satisfaction of) his money. According to Zufar, it becomes a pawn for one hundred, because the substitute remains to the extent of one-tenth, so the debt remains to that extent. We said to Zufar: that the second slave stands in the place of the first, so it becomes as if the first remained and its price returned [to its original]. Then for Muhammad: that the pawned (item) has changed in the possession of the mortgagee, so the pawner has an option like the sold item if it is killed before delivery. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): that the change did not manifest in respect of the slave because the second stands in his place. (Footnote 1: That is, the offending slave given in place of the killed slave due to his killing, the pawner redeems it with all his debt because the second stands in place of the first in flesh and blood. Refer to al-Durr al-Muntaqa 2:609. (2) al-'Inayah 10:191. (3) al-Kifayah 9:124-125.)
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a pawned slave killed by another slave worth 100. The killer slave is given as compensation (دفع به). Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that this compensation frees the pawn with all its debt (فك بكل دينه) – meaning the mortgagee accepts the substitute as full satisfaction. Muhammad holds that the pawner has an option: either to pay the debt and redeem the original pawn (though it is dead? Actually 'fakka' means to redeem the pawn by paying the debt, or to hand over the substitute to the mortgagee in satisfaction). Zufar holds that the substitute becomes a new pawn for only 100, keeping the debt alive for 900. The Hanafi response to Zufar is that the substitute stands in the place of the first fully, so it is as if the original remained and its price returned. Then the text explains Muhammad's reasoning by analogy to a sold item killed before delivery: the buyer has an option because the item has changed. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's reasoning is that the change did not manifest because the substitute is exactly like the original; hence no option. The footnotes elaborate: the substitute is equivalent in humanity and legal status, so the pawner cannot claim that the pawn has changed; hence his option is negated. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
دفع (dafʿ): Giving of the killer slave as compensation (بدل) for the killed pawn.
فك (fakk): Redemption of the pawn; freeing it from the debt by full satisfaction.
خيار (khiyār): Option granted to the pawner to choose between redeeming the pawn or handing over the substitute.
قيام مقام (qiyām maqām): Standing in place; the substitute is considered legally identical to the original.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what option does the pawner have when a pawned slave is killed by another slave and the killer slave is given as compensation?
A) He must accept the killer slave as full payment.
B) He may either redeem the pawn or give the killer slave to the mortgagee.
C) He loses all rights.
D) The debt is cancelled.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a substitute slave given as compensation fully redeems the pawn, with no option for the pawner.

Discharge of Debt When Killer Slave Replaces Slain Pledge
Intra-Hanafi dispute on full debt discharge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar on the discharge of a debt when a pledged slave is killed and the killer is substituted, and apply the Hanafi tarjih.

Core Idea
The substitute slave stands in full place of the original, so the debt is discharged — the trust nature of rahn blocks the analogy to sale.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya presents an intra-Hanafi dispute where the key question is whether compensating a killed pledge with the killer slave fully discharges the debt. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf argue yes, Muhammad and Zufar differ. We will analyze the proofs and see why the majority view prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and the dispute
Read the matn: 'If a slave worth a hundred killed him and he was compensated with it, the pledge is discharged with all of his debt.' This is the basic ruling. Note that the dispute is about whether this automatic discharge holds.
The commentary immediately signals ikhtilaf: 'this is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.'
2
State Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf's position and their proof
Their position: debt fully discharged. Proof: The second slave stands in the exact place of the first, both in form (a slave) and meaning (the killer is like the killed in humanity; both are equally subject to retaliation). The pledge is a trust (amana), so no ownership transfer occurs.
See the commentary on 'qa'im muqamahu' for the full justification.
3
State Muhammad's position and his qiyas
Muhammad: the pledgor has a choice — either ransom the substitute or surrender it to the mortgagee for the debt. He analogizes to a sold item killed before possession: the buyer has a choice to take the compensation or rescind.
The qiyas is based on 'change in the subject matter' (the pledge was destroyed).
4
State Zufar's partial view
Zufar: the substitute becomes a new pledge for only part of the debt (since only a fraction of the value is replaced), so the debt remains partially.
This is a minority view; the Hanafi response refutes it by arguing the second stands fully in place.
5
Recognize the Hanafi response and the mufta bihi
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) respond that the change is not legally apparent because the substitute is fully equivalent. The trust nature of the pledge prevents automatic transfer; the analogy to sale fails because sale involves ownership transfer, while pledge does not. The mufta bihi is the automatic discharge view.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah and al-Inayah favor this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(وإن قتله عبد يعدل مئة فدفع به فك بكل دينه) (۱) ، هذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ، وعند محمد : هو بالخيار إن شاء فكه ، وإن شاءَ سَلَّمَ العبد المدفوع إلى المرتهن بماله وعند زفرَ الله : يصير رهناً بمئة ؛ لأنه بقي الخلف بقدر العُشر، فيبقى الدين بقدره. قلنا لزفر الله : إنَّ العبد الثاني قائم مقامَ الأَوَّلِ فصار كما كان الأوَّلُ قائماً، وتراجع سعره. ثم لمحمد : أن المرهونَ تغيّر في ضمان المرتهن، فيخيرُ الرَّاهِنُ كالمبيع إذا قتل قبل القبض ، ولهما : أنّ التغير لم يظهر في حق العبد لقيام الثاني مقامه [۱] قوله : فك ؛ أي خلص الرهن بأداء كلّ دينه. [۲]قوله : قائماً ؛ مقام الأول صورة ومعنى، أما صورة فظاهر، وأما معنى فلان القاتل كالمقتول في الآدمية والشرع اعتبره حراً من حيث الآدمية دون المالية، ألا ترى إلى استوائهما في حق القصاص، فكذا في حق الدفع. كذا في «العناية). [۳] قوله : كالمبيع إذا قتل قبل القبض ؛ والمغصوب إذا قتل في يد الغاصب ؛ أي قتلهما عبد ودفع مكانهما، وإنّما قيد فيهما بالقتل ؛ لأنّ سعرهما لو نقص مما كان عليه وقت البيع والغصب لا خيار للمشتري والمغصوب منه ، بل يأخذهما من غير خيار. أما لو قتلهما عبد فدفع مكانهما يتخير المشتري بين أن يأخذ المدفوع بكل الثمن، وبين أن يفسخ البيع ؛ لتغير المبيع، وفي الغصب يتخيرُ المغصوب منه بين أن يأخذ المدفوع وبين أن يطالب الغاصب بقيمة المغصوب. هكذا في «الكفاية»(۳). [٤] قوله : لقيام الثاني مقامه ؛ كما ذكرناه آنفاً، وعين الرهن أمانة عند المرتهن عندنا، فلا يجوز تمليكه منه بغير رضاه ؛ ولأنّ جعل الرهن بالدين حكم جاهلي، وهو منسوخ بخلاف البيع ؛ لأنّ الخيار فيه حكمه الفسخ، وهو مشروع، وبخلاف الغصب ؛ لأن تملكه بأداء الضمان مشروع. (۳) (الكفاية» (۹: ١٢٤ - ١٢٥).
And if a slave worth a hundred killed him and he was compensated with it, the pledge is discharged with all of his debt. And if the debt remains, and the pledgor had ordered him to sell it for a hundred, the remainder is in his liability. (And if a slave worth a hundred killed him and he was compensated with it, the pledge is discharged with all of his debt) (1): this is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad: he has a choice; if he wishes, he may ransom it, and if he wishes, he may surrender the compensated slave to the mortgagee for his property. According to Zufar: it becomes a pledge for a hundred, because the replacement remains by the amount of a tenth, so the debt remains by its amount. We said to Zufar: Indeed, the second slave stands in the place of the first, so it becomes as if the first remained, and its value decreased. Then for Muhammad: The pledged property changed in the guarantee of the mortgagee, so the pledgor has a choice, like a sold item if it is killed before possession. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): The change did not become apparent regarding the slave because the second stands in his place. [1] He said: 'discharged' meaning the pledge is freed by paying all of his debt. [2] He said: 'standing' in place of the first in form and meaning. As for form, it is apparent; as for meaning, because the killer is like the killed in humanity, and the law considered the killer as free with respect to humanity, not wealth. Do you not see that they are equal in respect of retaliation? Likewise in respect of compensation. Thus in al-Inayah. [3] He said: 'like a sold item if it is killed before possession' and the usurped property if it is killed in the hand of the usurper; i.e., a slave kills them and is given in their place. He only restricted it by killing, because if their value decreased from what it was at the time of sale and usurpation, the buyer and the owner of the usurped property have no choice; rather, they take them without choice. But if a slave kills them and is given in their place, the buyer has a choice between taking the compensated slave for the full price and rescinding the sale due to the change in the sold item, and in usurpation, the owner of the usurped property has a choice between taking the compensated slave and suing the usurper for the value of the usurped property. Thus in al-Kifayah. [4] He said: 'because the second stands in his place' as we mentioned earlier, and the essence of the pledge is a trust with the mortgagee according to us, so he may not transfer ownership from it without his consent; and because making the pledge for the debt is a pre-Islamic custom and is abrogated, unlike sale because the choice in it is to rescind, which is legislated; and unlike usurpation, because taking ownership by paying a guarantee is legislated. (1) i.e., the pledgor ransoms the offending slave given in place of the slain slave for all his debt, because the second stands in the place of the first in flesh and blood. See al-Durr al-Muntaqa 2:609. (2) al-Inayah 10:191. (3) al-Kifayah 9:124-125.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the discharge of a debt when a slave that was given as a pledge (rahn) is killed, and the killer slave is given as compensation. The matn states the basic ruling: if the killer slave is worth a hundred (i.e., equal to the debt), the debt is fully discharged. The commentary elaborates the differing opinions of the major Hanafi imams. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the debt is automatically discharged because the second slave stands in the exact place of the first, both in form (as a slave) and in meaning (the killer is considered like the killed in humanity, thus legally equivalent for compensation). Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees: since the pledged property changed (the original slave is gone), the pledgor has a choice—either to ransom the new slave (pay the debt) or to surrender it to the mortgagee for the debt amount. He analogizes to the case where a sold item is killed before possession; there, the buyer also has a choice. Zufar ibn Hudhayl holds that the new slave becomes a new pledge for the remaining debt because only a tenth of the value was replaced, so the debt remains partially. The Hanafi response (presumably of the majority) argues that the second slave fully stands in the first's place, and the change is not legally significant because the substitute is exactly equivalent. The footnotes further clarify: 'fakk' means freeing the pledge by full payment; the substitute stands in every respect; the analogy to sale and usurpation is used by Muhammad but refuted because in pledge the mortgagee does not own the property—it is an amana (trust). The pre-Islamic practice of making the pledge itself property upon default is abrogated. Thus, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the debt is fully discharged.

Key Terms
فك (fakk): Discharge or release of the pledge (rahn) upon full payment of the debt.
قائم مقامه (qa'im muqamahu): Standing in his place, i.e., the second slave is legally equivalent to the first in all respects.
ضمان المرتهن (daman al-murtahin): Guarantee of the mortgagee; the responsibility for the pledge while in the mortgagee's possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what happens to the debt when a slave-in-pledge is killed and the killer is given as compensation?
A) The debt remains partially due.
B) The debt is fully discharged.
C) The pledgor has a choice to either ransom the killer slave or surrender it.
D) The killer becomes a new pledge for the same debt.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school (majority of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) holds that a substitute slave of equal value fully replaces the killed pledge, automatically discharging the debt.

Ransom of Pledge for Homicide by Mistake
Ruling on mortgagee's duty and pledgor's options for a slave-in-pledge's homicide by mistake

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mortgagee's obligation to ransom a slave-in-pledge that commits homicide by mistake, and explain the rationale of guarantee (daman) and the effect on the debt.

Core Idea
The mortgagee must ransom the pledge for a mistake homicide because the slave is under his guarantee; he cannot recover the cost.

In this passage, we examine a nuanced ruling from the Hanafi school on the liability of the mortgagee (murtehin) when a slave-in-pledge (rahn) commits a homicide by mistake. The passage clarifies the legal consequences: the mortgagee must pay the blood money (diyah) to ransom the slave, and if he refuses, the pledgor (rahin) has options that ultimately discharge the debt. The key principle is that the slave is in the mortgagee's guarantee (daman), making him responsible for damages caused by the slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific event? The slave-in-pledge commits a homicide by mistake. The ruling: the mortgagee must ransom the slave (pay the diyah) and cannot recover from the pledgor.
2
Locate the dalil and the legal reasoning
The proof is rational (aqli): the slave is in the mortgagee's guarantee (daman). Therefore, he is responsible for damages caused by the slave. The text explicitly states: 'because the slave is in his guarantee'.
The ruling is based on the general principle of guarantee, not a specific textual evidence.
3
Analyze the options when the mortgagee refuses
If the mortgagee refuses to ransom, the pledgor may either surrender the slave to the victim's family or ransom it himself. In both cases, the debt is discharged. If surrendered, it is treated as destruction in the mortgagee's guarantee; if ransomed, the debt is cleared via set-off (muqassah).
4
Understand the effect of set-off
When the pledgor ransoms, he pays the blood money on behalf of the mortgagee, creating a debt from mortgagee to pledgor equal to the ransom. That debt cancels the original mortgage debt through set-off (qisasan).
This prevents the pledgor from being a volunteer (mutabarri') because he acts to recover his own property.
5
Note the exception when the slave's value exceeds the debt
If the slave's value is greater than the debt, only the value of the slave drops from the debt, not the full debt. The remainder remains owed.
This is because the mortgagee's guarantee is limited to the slave's value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن جنى الرهن خطأ فداه مرتهنه ، ولم يرجع، فإن أبي دفعه الراهن أو فداه ، وسقط الدِّين، [1] قوله : فداه مرتهنه ؛ لأنّ العبد في ضمانه، فيقال للمرتهن : خذ العبد من الجناية، هذا إذا كان القيمة والدين سواء ، أما إذا كانت القيمة أكثر يسقط من الدين مقدار قيمة العبد، ولا يسقط الباقي، ولو فدى طهر المحل، فبقـى ديـن المرتهن على حاله ، ولم يرجع بشيء من ! الفداء على الراهن ؛ لأنّ الجناية حصلت في ضمان المرتهن، فكان عليه إصلاحها، ولا يملك المرتهن الدفع ؛ لأنه غير مالك، فلا يملك التمليك. [2]قوله : إن أبى ؛ أي المرتهن أن يفديه، قيل للراهن.... الخ ؛ لأنّ الملك في الرقبة قائم للراهن، وإنما يحكم إلى المرتهن بالفداء ؛ لقيام حقه، فإذا أنكر عن الفداء يطالب الراهن بحكم الجناية، ومن حكمها التخيير بين الدفع والفداء، فإن اختار الدفع سقط الدين ؛ لأنه استحق بمعنى في ضمان المرتهن ، فصار كالهلاك. وكذا إن اختار الفداء ؛ لأنَّ العبد كالحاصل له بعوض كان على المرتهن، وإذا كان على المرتهن فقد أداه الراهن، فيجب للراهن على المرتهن مثل ما أدى إلى ولي الجناية، وللمرتهن على الراهن دين، فالتقيا قصاصاً، فيسلم الرهن للراهن، ولا يكون الراهن متبرعاً في أداء الفداء ؛ لأنه يسعى في تخليص ملكه، كمصير الراهن. هكذا في «الهداية» وشروحها.
If the pledge commits a homicide by mistake, its mortgagee ransoms it, and does not recover. If he refuses, the pledgor surrenders it or ransoms it, and the debt drops. [1] He said: 'its mortgagee ransoms it' because the slave is in his guarantee; so it is said to the mortgagee: take the slave due to the homicide. This is when the value and the debt are equal. But if the value is more, only the amount of the slave's value drops from the debt, and the remainder does not drop. And if he ransoms, the place becomes pure, so the mortgagee's debt remains as is, and he does not recover anything from the ransom from the pledgor, because the homicide occurred in the mortgagee's guarantee, so he had to rectify it, and the mortgagee does not have the right to surrender (the slave) because he is not an owner, so he cannot transfer ownership. [2] He said: 'if he refuses', i.e., if the mortgagee refuses to ransom it, it is said to the pledgor... etc., because ownership of the slave remains with the pledgor, and the mortgagee is only ordered to ransom due to his right. So when he refuses the ransom, the pledgor is summoned due to the ruling of the homicide, and of its rulings is the choice between surrender and ransom. If he chooses surrender, the debt drops because it became due in the mortgagee's guarantee, so it is like destruction. Similarly, if he chooses ransom, because the slave is as if obtained for a compensation that was on the mortgagee, and if it was on the mortgagee, the pledgor has paid it, so the pledgor is owed by the mortgagee the like of what he paid to the guardian of the homicide, and the mortgagee has a debt on the pledgor, so they cancel each other by set-off, so the pledge is returned to the pledgor, and the pledgor is not a volunteer in paying the ransom because he seeks to retrieve his property, like the case of the mortgagor. Thus in al-Hidayah and its commentaries.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage deals with a case where the slave-in-pledge commits a homicide by mistake (khata'). The matn rules: the mortgagee (murtehin) must ransom the slave (pay the blood money) and cannot recover the cost from the pledgor. If the mortgagee refuses, the pledgor has the option to either surrender the slave to the victim's family or ransom it, and in either case the debt is discharged. The commentary explains the rationale: the slave is in the guarantee (daman) of the mortgagee, so he is responsible for damages caused by the slave. The mortgagee cannot surrender the slave because he is not an owner. If the mortgagee refuses, the pledgor steps in as the owner. If the pledgor chooses to ransom, the debt is discharged via set-off (muqassah): because the pledgor effectively paid the blood money on behalf of the mortgagee, creating a debt from the mortgagee to the pledgor equal to the ransom, which cancels the original debt. If the pledgor chooses to surrender the slave, it is as if the slave is destroyed in the mortgagee's guarantee, so the debt ceases. The text notes that if the slave's value exceeds the debt, only the value of the slave is deducted from the debt, not the full debt. This ruling is based on the principle that the slave is an amana in the mortgagee's hands, and any damage occurring during that trust liability is his responsibility.

Key Terms
جنى خطأ (jani khata'): Committing a homicide by mistake (unintentional killing).
فداه (fadah): Ransom; paying the blood money (diyah) to free the slave from liability.
قصاصاً (qisasan): By way of set-off (muqassah); the mutual debts cancel each other.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the mortgagee refuses to ransom a slave-in-pledge that committed homicide by mistake, what happens to the debt?
A) The debt remains and the mortgagee must pay the ransom later.
B) The pledgor must pay the ransom and the debt remains.
C) The pledgor may surrender the slave or ransom it, and the debt is discharged.
D) The mortgagee loses the debt immediately.

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee's guarantee (daman) of the pledge makes him liable to ransom it for accidental homicide, with no recourse to the pledgor, and the debt is discharged upon the pledgor's alternative actions.

Executor's Duty to Sell the Pledge Upon Pledgor's Death
Ruling on executor's duty to sell the pledge and pay the debt after pledgor's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the executor's obligation to sell the pledge upon the pledgor's death and apply it to a simple scenario.

Core Idea
Death does not extinguish the debt; the executor must sell the pledge to pay it.

When a person who has pledged property as security for a debt dies before the debt is paid, the pledged property does not automatically transfer to the mortgagee. Instead, the executor of the deceased is responsible for selling the pledge and using the proceeds to settle the debt. This lesson focuses on this concise ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering condition
The ruling applies when the pledgor (raahin) dies. Recognize that death is the event that activates the executor's duty.
The text begins with 'ولو مات الراهن' (and if the pledgor dies).
2
Identify the responsible party
The executor (wasi) of the deceased pledgor is the agent who must act. Understand that the executor represents the estate.
The term 'وصي' (wasi) is used.
3
Identify the required actions
The executor must perform two actions in sequence: first, sell the pledge (باع رهنه), then pay the debt (قضى دينه). Note the priority: the debt is paid from the sale proceeds.
The text uses 'باع' (sells) and 'قضى' (pays).
4
Consider implied outcomes
After paying the debt, any surplus from the sale goes to the pledgor's heirs. If the sale proceeds are insufficient, the remaining debt becomes a claim against the estate.
This step goes beyond the text but is essential for full understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو مات الرَّاهِنُ باعَ وصيه رهنه ، وقضى دينه
And if the pledgor dies, his executor sells his pledge and pays off his debt.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This is a concise ruling from the matn stating the procedure when the pledgor (raahin) dies before the debt is paid. The executor (wasi) of the pledgor is obligated to sell the pledged property (rahn) and use the proceeds to satisfy the debt owed to the mortgagee (murtehin). The commentary in the original text (not included here) would elaborate that the sale is conducted with the permission of the mortgagee, and any excess goes to the pledgor's heirs, while any shortfall remains a claim against the estate. This ruling is based on the principle that the pledge is a security for the debt, and upon death, the executor represents the deceased's interests.

Key Terms
وصي (wasi): Executor of the deceased's will; the person appointed to manage the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
